id="article-contents"><div class="MarkdownContent_markdownBody__v5MYy markdown-body"><h2 id="about-api-versioning" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#about-api-versioning">About API versioning<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h2>
<p>The GitHub REST API is versioned. The API version name is based on the date when the API version was released. For example, the API version <code>2026-03-10</code> was released on Tue, 10 Mar 2026.</p>
<p>Breaking changes are changes that can potentially break an integration. Breaking changes will be released in a new API version. We will provide advance notice before releasing breaking changes. Breaking changes include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Removing an entire operation</li>
<li>Removing or renaming a parameter</li>
<li>Removing or renaming a response field</li>
<li>Adding a new required parameter</li>
<li>Making a previously optional parameter required</li>
<li>Changing the type of a parameter or response field</li>
<li>Removing enum values</li>
<li>Adding a new validation rule to an existing parameter</li>
<li>Changing authentication or authorization requirements</li>
</ul>
<p>Any additive (non-breaking) changes will be available in all supported API versions. Additive changes are changes that should not break an integration. Additive changes include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Adding an operation</li>
<li>Adding an optional parameter</li>
<li>Adding an optional request header</li>
<li>Adding a response field</li>
<li>Adding a response header</li>
<li>Adding enum values</li>
</ul>
<p>When a new REST API version is released, the previous API version will be supported for at least 24 more months following the release of the new API version.</p>
<h2 id="specifying-an-api-version" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#specifying-an-api-version">Specifying an API version<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h2>
<p>You should use the <code>X-GitHub-Api-Version</code> header to specify an API version. For example:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl --header "X-GitHub-Api-Version:2026-03-10" https://api.github.com/zen
</code></pre>
<p>Requests without the <code>X-GitHub-Api-Version</code> header will default to use the <code>2022-11-28</code> version.</p>
<p>If you specify an API version that is no longer supported, you will receive a <code>410 Gone</code> response.</p>
<h2 id="upgrading-to-a-new-api-version" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#upgrading-to-a-new-api-version">Upgrading to a new API version<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h2>
<p>Before upgrading to a new REST API version, you should read the changelog of breaking changes for the new API version to understand what breaking changes are included and to learn more about how to upgrade to that specific API version. For more information, see <a href="/en/rest/overview/breaking-changes">Breaking changes</a>.</p>
<p>When you update your integration to specify the new API version in the <code>X-GitHub-Api-Version</code> header, you'll also need to make any changes required for your integration to work with the new API version.</p>
<p>Once your integration is updated, test your integration to verify that it works with the new API version.</p>
<h2 id="api-version-closing-down" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#api-version-closing-down">API version closing down<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h2>
<p>API versions are supported for 24 months after a newer API version is released.</p>
<p>While a version is within its support window but approaching  closing down, GitHub includes the following headers in API responses to help you prepare for migration:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>Deprecation</code> — The date when the API version will be closing down, formatted as an HTTP date per <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7231#section-7.1.1.1">RFC 7231</a>. For example: <code>Wed, 27 Nov 2019 14:34:29 GMT</code>. </li>
<li><code>Sunset</code> — The date when the API version will be completely removed (retired), after which requests will return a <code>410 Gone</code> response. Follows <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc8594">RFC 8594</a>. For example: <code>Fri, 27 Nov 2020 14:34:29 GMT</code>. </li>
</ul>
<p>After the support window ends:</p>
<ul>
<li>Requests that specify a closing down API version receive a <code>410 Gone</code> response.</li>
<li>Requests that do not specify an API version default to the next oldest supported version, not the closing down version. If you rely on unversioned requests, you may observe behavioral changes as older versions are removed from support.</li>
</ul>
<p>For more information on migrating to a newer API version, see <a href="/en/rest/about-the-rest-api/breaking-changes">Breaking changes</a>.</p>
<h2 id="exceptions-to-standard-versioning" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#exceptions-to-standard-versioning">Exceptions to standard versioning<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h2>
<p>In rare cases, GitHub may make changes outside the normal API versioning cadence. These are exceptional interventions that do not alter the standard versioning guarantees for most integrators.</p>
<h3 id="security-availability-and-reliability-issues" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#security-availability-and-reliability-issues">Security, availability, and reliability issues<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h3>
<p>Critical security vulnerabilities, data exposure risks, or severe reliability issues may require changes outside the normal release schedule. GitHub may release an unscheduled API version, backport fixes to supported versions, or in rare cases, introduce a breaking change to an existing version to protect users and platform integrity.</p>
<p>GitHub will communicate such changes through release notes, changelogs, and direct communication explaining what changed and why. Where feasible, advance notice will be provided. Immediate action may be taken without advance notice when required.</p>
<h3 id="low-usage-services" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#low-usage-services">Low-usage services<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h3>
<p>For certain services with very low usage, GitHub may deprecate functionality outside the standard versioning process. In these cases, GitHub will communicate the intent and reach out to affected integrators directly.</p>
<h2 id="supported-api-versions" tabindex="-1"><a class="heading-link" href="#supported-api-versions">Supported API versions<span class="heading-link-symbol" aria-hidden="true"></span></a></h2>
<p>The following REST API versions are currently supported.</p>

















<table aria-labelledby="supported-api-versions"><thead><tr><th scope="col">API version</th><th scope="col">End of support date</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>2026-03-10</code></td><td>Not yet scheduled</td></tr><tr><td><code>2022-11-28</code></td><td>March 10, 2028</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>You can also make an API request to get all of the supported API versions. For more information, see <a href="/en/rest/meta/meta#get-all-api-versions">REST API endpoints for meta data</a>.</p></div></div></div></div></div></main><footer data-container="footer"><section Versions","intro":"\u003cp\u003eLearn how to specify which REST API version to use whenever you make a request to the REST API.\u003c/p\u003e","effectiveDate":"","renderedPage":"\u003ch2 id=\"about-api-versioning\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#about-api-versioning\"\u003eAbout API versioning\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe GitHub REST API is versioned. The API version name is based on the date when the API version was released. For example, the API version \u003ccode\u003e2026-03-10\u003c/code\u003e was released on Tue, 10 Mar 2026.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBreaking changes are changes that can potentially break an integration. Breaking changes will be released in a new API version. We will provide advance notice before releasing breaking changes. Breaking changes include:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRemoving an entire operation\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRemoving or renaming a parameter\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRemoving or renaming a response field\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding a new required parameter\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eMaking a previously optional parameter required\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eChanging the type of a parameter or response field\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRemoving enum values\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding a new validation rule to an existing parameter\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eChanging authentication or authorization requirements\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAny additive (non-breaking) changes will be available in all supported API versions. Additive changes are changes that should not break an integration. Additive changes include:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding an operation\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding an optional parameter\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding an optional request header\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding a response field\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding a response header\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAdding enum values\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen a new REST API version is released, the previous API version will be supported for at least 24 more months following the release of the new API version.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"specifying-an-api-version\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#specifying-an-api-version\"\u003eSpecifying an API version\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou should use the \u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e header to specify an API version. For example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003ecurl --header \"X-GitHub-Api-Version:2026-03-10\" https://api.github.com/zen\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eRequests without the \u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e header will default to use the \u003ccode\u003e2022-11-28\u003c/code\u003e version.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you specify an API version that is no longer supported, you will receive a \u003ccode\u003e410 Gone\u003c/code\u003e response.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"upgrading-to-a-new-api-version\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#upgrading-to-a-new-api-version\"\u003eUpgrading to a new API version\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBefore upgrading to a new REST API version, you should read the changelog of breaking changes for the new API version to understand what breaking changes are included and to learn more about how to upgrade to that specific API version. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/breaking-changes\"\u003eBreaking changes\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen you update your integration to specify the new API version in the \u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e header, you'll also need to make any changes required for your integration to work with the new API version.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOnce your integration is updated, test your integration to verify that it works with the new API version.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"api-version-closing-down\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#api-version-closing-down\"\u003eAPI version closing down\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAPI versions are supported for 24 months after a newer API version is released.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile a version is within its support window but approaching  closing down, GitHub includes the following headers in API responses to help you prepare for migration:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDeprecation\u003c/code\u003e — The date when the API version will be closing down, formatted as an HTTP date per \u003ca href=\"https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7231#section-7.1.1.1\"\u003eRFC 7231\u003c/a\u003e. For example: \u003ccode\u003eWed, 27 Nov 2019 14:34:29 GMT\u003c/code\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSunset\u003c/code\u003e — The date when the API version will be completely removed (retired), after which requests will return a \u003ccode\u003e410 Gone\u003c/code\u003e response. Follows \u003ca href=\"https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc8594\"\u003eRFC 8594\u003c/a\u003e. For example: \u003ccode\u003eFri, 27 Nov 2020 14:34:29 GMT\u003c/code\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAfter the support window ends:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRequests that specify a closing down API version receive a \u003ccode\u003e410 Gone\u003c/code\u003e response.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRequests that do not specify an API version default to the next oldest supported version, not the closing down version. If you rely on unversioned requests, you may observe behavioral changes as older versions are removed from support.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information on migrating to a newer API version, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/about-the-rest-api/breaking-changes\"\u003eBreaking changes\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"exceptions-to-standard-versioning\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#exceptions-to-standard-versioning\"\u003eExceptions to standard versioning\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn rare cases, GitHub may make changes outside the normal API versioning cadence. These are exceptional interventions that do not alter the standard versioning guarantees for most integrators.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"security-availability-and-reliability-issues\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#security-availability-and-reliability-issues\"\u003eSecurity, availability, and reliability issues\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCritical security vulnerabilities, data exposure risks, or severe reliability issues may require changes outside the normal release schedule. GitHub may release an unscheduled API version, backport fixes to supported versions, or in rare cases, introduce a breaking change to an existing version to protect users and platform integrity.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGitHub will communicate such changes through release notes, changelogs, and direct communication explaining what changed and why. Where feasible, advance notice will be provided. Immediate action may be taken without advance notice when required.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"low-usage-services\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#low-usage-services\"\u003eLow-usage services\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor certain services with very low usage, GitHub may deprecate functionality outside the standard versioning process. In these cases, GitHub will communicate the intent and reach out to affected integrators directly.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"supported-api-versions\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#supported-api-versions\"\u003eSupported API versions\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe following REST API versions are currently supported.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u003ctable aria-labelledby=\"supported-api-versions\"\u003e\u003cthead\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eAPI version\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eEnd of support date\u003c/th\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/thead\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e2026-03-10\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eNot yet scheduled\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e2022-11-28\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eMarch 10, 2028\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/tbody\u003e\u003c/table\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can also make an API request to get all of the supported API versions. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/meta/meta#get-all-api-versions\"\u003eREST API endpoints for meta
